RATING: 9.1
Admito que joguei esse jogo a primeira vez ainda com um certo preconceito. Participo com uma certa frequência de um evento semanal e, nesse evento, o ranking sempre o colocava no TOP 5, as vezes TOP 3, e eu me perguntava como um jogo de dados relativamente recente poderia ser tão bom a ponto de rivalizar com clássicos como Terra Mystica, Agricola e Power Grid e até mesmo maravilhas recentes, como Mombasa, Caledonia e GWT, todos sem a "cruz" do fator sorte que os dados sempre carregam.
Então, jogar Marco Polo me respondeu plenamente o fascínio que ele exerce em alguns. Eita jogo bom! Apesar dos dados, as mecânicas são tão bem feitas que sua sorte é bastante mitigada. Pelo contrário, os dados dão um charme ao jogo, tanto que, dos personagens q conheci, o que me dá menos vontade de jogar é justamente aquele q não joga os dados, apenas coloca os números de sua escolha. Acredito que isso tire bastante do desafio e exercício mental (q, em essência, pra mim são, afinal, duas das grandes diversões de se jogar board games) de otimizar as ações com base nos valores que saíram.
E por falar em personagens... Que personagens! Muitos dirão que alguns são muito roubados, mas está justamente aí o trunfo do jogo: TODOS ELES são roubados! Isso fornece um equilíbrio maravilhoso (levando em conta que conheci apenas os 4 personagens iniciais). Ao contrário de, por exemplo, Terra Mystica, onde os poderes das raças só aparecem em situações específicas ao longo do jogo, ou Small World, onde, dependendo da partida, uma mesma raça pode ser muito poderosa ou muito ruim, ou até mesmo Colt Express, onde personagens são nitidamente muito mais poderosos que outros qq q seja a situação (sorry pelo exemplo meia boca, não tenho tantos jogos de poderes variáveis assim), em Marco Polo, os poderes são todos ótimos e podem ser usados potencialmente em todos os turnos (mais uma vez, conheci apenas com os 4 personagens do setup básico, sei que existem outros que variam bastante, inclusive quero conhecê-los).
Por fim, as possibilidades estratégicas são ótimas e a variedade é bem presente, com as cartas e contratos dos mais diversos, dando uma rejogabilidade fora do comum. Não está isento de problemas, ouvi dizer que as vezes é possível ganhar sem fazer uma viagem sequer. Os tokens grandes tb são ruins, com pouca diferença para os pequenos, oq confunde os jogadores. Mas no mínimo já entra no meu top 20 e com certeza quero jogá-lo de novo, com outros personagens e acredito q tem qualidades para me ganhar mais ainda e se consolidar no meu top 10 ou até, quem sabe, top 5.

RATING: 6
Interesting dice-as-worker-placement game, yet another entry in the heavy Euros that seem to dominate the hobby game scene nowadays.  The theme here is better than in most, as there's a travel and a trading goods aspect that feels right, though there are still places where the theme is very grafted on.  The variable player powers here are a great touch, one that with this game and [gameid=120677], Euros seem to finally be willing to embrace in a way that's more than a minor tweak.  The mechanics of this game are not especially unique, but they are solid, and I expect this one will stick around for at least a little while.

RATING: 6
"Terra Mystica lite" is a pretty apt description of Marco Polo, as you formulate a strategy at the outset based on the random setup of the board and the character you choose. There isn't as much spatial interaction as in TM, but there is an interesting traveling salesman problem to solve (unique every time based on the setup). The game also has a fair amount of turn angst from the dice placement mechanism: while you often aren't entirely shut out from taking an action if someone else takes it, you do have to pay a penalty that could be very costly to your efficiency. Overall I really like it- the inter-game variability is pretty high which keeps things relatively fresh. This delivers quite strongly for a medium-weight, 90 minute game. Perhaps best with 3 just cause itt'l take less time than with 4.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
I held off on this one as no one seemed to be covering it and that's typically a clue that it's not worth playing. However, Tom Vasel reviewed it and my co-worker was telling me about it as well, so I gave it a shot.

In [b]The Voyages of Marco Polo[/b] you're tasked with earning victory points by acquiring goods and money and fulfilling contracts. In that way, it's almost like playing [b]Lords of Waterdeep[/b]. However, you also need to move across Asia in order to go to different towns to setup your trade routes and acquire goods. 

The way you'll be doing all of this is by rolling dice and then placing them on the available actions: gain money, gain trade goods, travel, take contracts, take a good and some camels. You'll be placing one or more dice on these actions and then taking what you're owed. These dice determine the "strength" of your selected action, typically allowing you to gain more or do more of something, with the lowest die determining how much. In addition, most spaces can be used by multiple players if they pay money equal to the lowest die being placed, so you're never completely shut off from the various actions you may need.

Finally, each player has a role card that "breaks" the game in some interesting way. I say "breaks" because they all seem broken in their own unique way: not having to roll dice, getting another die and contract each turn, starting at the end position on the map, traveling easier, and so on. Without these, the game would be fine, but with these it really kicks it up a notch. Asymmetry always makes me appreciate a game just that much more.

This is definitely a game I recommend playing and picking up if any of the above sounds interesting to you. If you're interested in theme, I feel like this game does a pretty good job of giving you a theme, even if it's a little thin when looking at the actions.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.9
Tremendous game in terms of mechanics, art work/display, theme, decision making and satisfaction at the end of the game.  Love the asymmetric starting powers!  This helps decide the individual strategies.  Another bonus is the relative quick play-time. A step up from Stone age and TTR, and a slice below the heavy-weight games like Terra Mystica and Yedo (which are both excellent games too).

RATING: N/A
Dice worker placement network builder depicting the young Marco Polo's expedition along the Silk Road to Kublai Khan. Players roll worker action pool dice to buy gold, gain Khan's favor, and collect goods and camels to fulfill, contracts.  Travel around the Silk Road and build trade houses along the way. The fun and addiction comes from leveraging your special character power with the standard bonus actions and claimed seeded city bonus tiles while completing contracts.

RATING: 8
After the first play it left me feeling disappointed. Perhaps I was hoping for too much because of all the hype around the game, but still the fact remains that the game leaves you feeling like you didn't get enough time to accomplish what you wanted (some goals are impossible to achieve other than with certain characters and while neglecting other goals).

However, there is something in this game that makes me want to play it more (perhaps the actual toughness of some goals). Also, I think the game will yield you a lot of plays because of the huge variety in the setup and different characters to play. So, overall I am glad to own it and I think it's a very good game in the end.

For 1-2 testing plays with friends - not recommended
For owning and playing it dozens of time - highly recommended

It reminds me of Stone Age for some reason, though Stone Age is way more elegant (both graphically and mechanically), is more streamlined and brings way bigger satisfaction (you can score 300-something points, whereas in Marco Polo you can end up having 30-something points).
I think I prefer Stone Age in general, but I believe this game offers higher replayability. So in the end, both games end up with the same score.

RATING: 9.5
Theme/Art:
The art is not outstanding, but the game looks good and I really enjoy the theme. The game board and the general design of the game are very good and clear.

Production quality:
Thick cardboard for all tiles, wooden pieces for the resources, and pretty big wooden dice for your workers. So the very good. I love that the money has different shapes and sizes for  each amount and it's not only round coins.

Replayability:
Very high. There are 8 characters with different abilities (all sound very strong, but if every character is strong, none is), many different action spaces for the big cities, which are assigned randomly, many different missions and orders for the players, so each game is different. Only the small town bonuses are the same each game.

Depth/Difficulty:
It's not the easiest game, but not the hardest either. I think I can explain it in about 10 to 15 minutes to new players. The game is quite deep, especially because you only have 5 rounds to reach all your goals and complete all missions. It is not a very long game, but you have to think ahead a lot. If you are the first to take an action space you may get money from others using the space later in the same round, but you may have to pay others on other spots.
I weight it 3/5.

Strategy:
This game is all about strategy. From the selection of your character, over the selection of your missions and the route you travel to the actions you take each turn, everything affects your performance in this game.

Luck:
Even though you roll dice as your workers there is no such thing as a bad dice roll (well, there is, if you only roll low or only high it can be bad). Low dice don't give you high rewards on action spaces, but you have to pay your opponents less for using the action space.
The setup is random and the orders for each round are random too, but visible once laid out. I would say that the game has low luck.

The Voyages of Marco Polo takes about 20-25 minutes per player, so the information on the box is correct.

I enjoyed the game very much and so did everybody I played it with. It's deep and strategic, yet you don't have to commit your whole evening to playing it.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8.25
This is a game that came out of nowhere for me. There was a bit of buzz about it on the geek so I decided to check it out. The more I read about it, the more that I really wanted it.

Having only played it twice so far... I'm happy that I jumped on the chance to grab it... minor mistakes in the first printing and all. 

It is like the designers built a game based on all of the mechanisms that I love. You roll dice at the beginning of each round, similar to Castles of Burgundy, and that determines the type of actions/resources/etc. that you can get each turn. These dice can be manipulated as well. You have resource conversion and contract fulfillment. There's an exploration/travelling aspect that opens more options for you throughout the game and/or gives you benefits each round... and end game points if you complete your secret objective cards. These mechanics on their own would have combined to make an interesting game but layer on top of that the variable character powers that all seem to be overpowered in their own right and break the rules of the game and it's AWESOME!

Every turn has you agonize over what you should be doing to maximize your return. The fact that other players can jack the spot you wanted, making it more expensive for you to take that action or completely block it off from you at all, necessitates that you keep strategic options open. You also need to understand what your player's strengths are and how to benefit from them... just so many moving parts, so many options, so many strategies... I can't say enough about it.

With so many variables to the game's setup, replayability is through the roof. The fact that we played a 4-player "learning game" in about 2 hours is amazing. Can't say enough about this game.

RATING: 8.3
This is quite a well designed game!  I love how the game requires that you analyze the board ahead of time.  I hate how the game requires you to analyze the board ahead of time!  It's a love hate relationship with that aspect of the game because if you don't analyze the board before you choose characters, you could set yourself up for failure.  This could draw players away from the incredible gameplay.  The dice allocation system is really clever and tense.  The spaces on the board are limited and it's first come, first served unless you are willing to pay more.  I think its absolutely brilliant how the designer was able to create individual player power characters that feel incredibly strong and satisfying.  You will feel like your opponents power is SO strong and they will fell the same about yours. Its nice that there are multiple paths to scoring points (contracts, travel, board spaces that give points).  A real gem of a game and I can't see myself selling this for a long time!

Note: Sleeved with Game Plus Premium mini euro sleeves.
